Last Year's Customs Revenue Decreased

Mr. Meyer-Harling is Scheduled to Go South to Inspect Various Customs Offices

After the eastern provinces were occupied by the Japanese army, the national customs revenue decreased. Now Meyer-Harling, the Inspector General of Customs, plans to go south to inspect various customs offices on the 11th and 12th of this month to reorganize them. The various news items are divided and sent to the following:

General Overview of the Decrease

The situation of the national customs revenue in the Republic of China in 1921 has now been reported by the Inspector General of Customs to the Ministry of Finance and will be publicly announced. The exact number cannot be ascertained, but its general situation is indeed less than before, because the Northeast customs duties were seized by the Japanese. It is said that the situation of the decrease is slightly less than the tax revenue of the three northeastern provinces before. According to the number of Northeast tax revenues announced by Finance Minister Song Ziwen last year, the average annual revenue is 39 million yuan.

Meyer Will Go South

Meyer-Harling, the Inspector General of Customs, went to various places in the north for inspection in October last year in order to inspect the customs administration and tax revenue situation in various places. Now it is learned that Mr. Meyer is now scheduled to leave Shanghai on the 11th and 12th of this month and go south to inspect the coastal ports of Zhejiang, Fujian, Guangdong, Macau and Hong Kong, and is scheduled to return to Shanghai in two weeks.

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Delegation Returns from Beijing to Petition

Request to Open the Intercepting Dam

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce last year repeatedly received letters from the Miscellaneous Grains Association requesting that the Construction Bureau be appealed to open the intercepting dam. Considering the matter to be of great importance, it was deemed necessary to petition the provincial government. A resolution was passed at a standing committee meeting to appoint Executive Committee member Zheng Zenan as a representative, along with representatives of the industry, to petition the provincial government. These representatives have now returned to Shanghai. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency made a special trip to interview them and obtained the following information. "I was appointed by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce as a representative, along with Mr. Wang Muyi, representative of the Miscellaneous Grains Association, to petition the Construction Bureau to open the intercepting dam. The reason is that the harvest of miscellaneous grains in northern Jiangsu this year has been very abundant. Local grain merchants transport them to Shanghai, usually via the Grand Canal. However, due to the intercepting dam between Gaoyou and Baoying not being open, they have to detour through Mapeng Bay. Since the beginning of winter, there has been a prolonged drought, and the water in Mapeng Bay is too shallow for navigation. They must still take the Grand Canal directly. We appealed to the Construction Bureau to open the intercepting dam, and they immediately instructed the River Works Bureau to handle it. However, the River Works Bureau stated that there are still over 300 zhang of siltation near the intercepting dam, which must be dredged first before the dam can be opened. However, there are 3,000 to 4,000 cargo ships waiting urgently to go south, with a cargo value of approximately 5 to 6 million. All must arrive in Shanghai before the final settlement of accounts. If they cannot arrive on time, the impact on Shanghai's finance will be significant. Furthermore, the cargo ships are stranded there, and each ship requires daily food expenses, which are substantial. They will inevitably have to exchange goods for money to maintain their livelihoods, and the loss to passengers and cargo is incalculable. Therefore, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce believes that the matter is of great importance and that it is necessary to petition Beijing. Thus, I went to the province on the evening of December 29th and visited Director Dong of the Construction Bureau the next morning, explaining everything in detail. Director Dong also believed that the dam should be opened urgently to alleviate the difficulty. He immediately instructed Section Chief Xu to inform the River Works Bureau by telegram. He also instructed us to go to Yangzhou to meet with Director Xu Dingchang of the River Works Bureau and urge him to open the dam quickly. Thereupon, we crossed the river on the morning of the 31st and transferred to a long-distance bus to Yangzhou. We met with Director Xu and requested him to open the dam quickly to save the merchants from their predicament and the livelihoods of thousands of boatmen. Director Xu replied that he had just taken over the post and that this kind of harm to merchants was a mistake made by his predecessor. Now that the dredging work at the siltation site has begun, it is difficult to stop. This project employs over 2,000 people and should be completed within about a week. Since merchants are eager to open the dam, they should send someone again to supervise and urge the matter so that the dam can be opened as soon as possible." With Director Xu's sincere reply, it is estimated that the dam can be opened by around the 10th of this month at the latest. Therefore, this trip is considered satisfactory.

Amendment of Diesel Fuel Tax Rate

Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Luo Fude, Tax Commissioner, issued Joint Proclamation No. 1268, which stated, "Regarding the Joint Proclamation, the Ministry of Finance has ordered that Article 491 of the current Customs Import Tariff of the Republic of China should be amended as follows: 'Original text: Diesel fuel, 2.90 gold units per ton. Note: For diesel fuel imported for manufacturing and refining purposes, an additional tax of 23.40 gold units per ton shall be levied in addition to the original tax rate.' This shall take effect from January 5th of this year, and compliance is required." In accordance with this order, we must comply. The regulations for the management of transporting diesel fuel for refining kerosene have also been established. Copies of these regulations are available directly from this customs office. All merchants are hereby notified. This proclamation is hereby issued."

Party and Government Agencies Mediate the Labor Dispute at British American Tobacco Factories

A Solution Has Been Decided; Work Will Resume Tomorrow

Fourteen child laborers in the box-making section of the new British American Tobacco factory in Pudong went on strike because the employer failed to fulfill the reconciliation record No. 334 of the Social Affairs Bureau. Due to the interconnectedness of all sections, the strike of the child laborers affected more than 4,000 workers, who were all unable to work. To prevent the escalation of the labor dispute, the Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters have been actively trying to mediate for several days. They also summoned Li Deke (transliteration), a representative of the employer, for persuasion. At 10 a.m. yesterday, the Social Affairs Bureau sent Wang Gang from the Third Section, along with Zhang Sheng, the general secretary of the Municipal Party Headquarters, to Pudong to mediate. An agreement was reached by representatives of both labor and management yesterday, and a specific solution was decided: (1) The employer shall comply with the reconciliation record, "The factory shall increase the wages of the workers in the new factory's box-making section, starting from December 1st of this year (i.e., the 21st year of the Republic), as per the usual practice." (2) Workers in the new factory shall resume work uniformly on the morning of the 9th. (3) The difference of one person in the number of workers in the new factory's box-making section shall be resolved separately. The Fifth District Cigarette Industry Union has already notified workers to resume work uniformly on the 9th.

The Chinese Ratepayers Association Asks the Municipal Council to Explain the Hotel Licensing Regulations

Disparate Treatment Between Chinese and Foreigners; A Lack of Fairness

The Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Public Settlement sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating, "Regarding the matter of applying for a liquor license for Western restaurants in the central district of the Public Settlement, the Daxia Hotel has stated that it has negotiated with the Municipal Council. According to the official, except for existing hotels that already have licenses, new restaurants will not be allowed to apply for them. This kind of regulation is unfair and has many drawbacks. Here are some points of concern: (1) Can the existing licenses be transferred? (2) Can the existing licenses be passed down through generations? (3) Is there a time limit for the existing licenses? (4) Is the issuance of licenses related to nationality? If licenses can be transferred, it is akin to a monopoly. If they can be passed down through generations, they become private property. If licenses have no time limit, the right to sell alcohol will permanently belong to a few. Now, foreign restaurants all have licenses and are close to each other, while Chinese merchants are deliberately hindered. How can this be considered fair? If the Municipal Council is truly concerned about maintaining local order, it can impose restrictions on the time for selling alcohol, such as prohibiting the sale of alcohol before 6 p.m. etc. The current method of issuing liquor licenses can lead to the conclusions drawn by the hotel. If there is different treatment between Chinese and foreigners, it violates the principle of impartiality by the authorities. In light of the aforementioned, we respectfully request that your board consider this matter further and provide a satisfactory explanation." To the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Settlement.

Sales Results of Charity Horse Race Tickets

To Conclude on the 10th of This Month

The charity horse race tickets issued recently in this city have been purchased very enthusiastically. All sales outlets are overwhelmed. According to experienced observers, it was known that they would be sold out. Yesterday, a reporter from the Central News Agency inquired about the situation with the Municipal Finance Bureau. An official made the following remarks: (1) The process of entrusting sales outlets for promotion: The horse race for charity fundraising was made possible with the support of the Shanghai Race Club, the Chinese Sports Association, the International Sports Association, and various gentlemen and merchants in this city. This is gratifying. However, the matter pertains to fundraising in the urban area, and the promotion of tickets is an obligation of the Finance Bureau. The method of promotion requires collective effort. Therefore, at the beginning, we consulted with various banks, companies, newspapers, organizations, and agencies in this city to serve as sales outlets. Initially, there were only over 30, and later more than 10 others joined, totaling over 40. This shows the enthusiasm and support of all sectors. (2) Number of tickets sold: The number of tickets issued was 110,000, of which 10,000 were complimentary. As of the 6th of this month, the Finance Bureau had received 86,500 tickets and 8,620 complimentary tickets from the Shanghai Race Club for distribution to various sales outlets. Most sales outlets have sold out all of their tickets, and a few others have very few tickets left. The Shanghai Race Club also has only about 1,000 tickets left, which should be sold out in two or three days. (5) Collection and remittance of ticket revenue: The ticket revenue transferred by the Finance Bureau to the Shanghai Race Club, including advance payments and remittances upon receipt, will be equivalent to the number of tickets received. The remaining ticket revenue is being collected from various sales outlets in recent days and will be remitted successively. According to another source, the Finance Bureau's handling of the promotion of tickets is scheduled to conclude on the 10th of this month. The calculation of ticket revenue and other procedures are very complicated and must be concluded a few days earlier. Sales outlets, except those who received tickets with cash, will have their remaining tickets collected uniformly for alternative sales methods. It is also reported that the Finance Bureau has issued a circular to all sales outlets.

Board of Directors of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation

Resolves to Purchase Three Junkers Aircraft

Employees Suspended from Duty Will Be Given Consolation Money

The Eurasia Aviation Corporation held its 18th Board of Directors meeting at the company at 6 p.m. the day before yesterday. The directors present were Wei Yifu, Li Jingcong, Shen Yani, Lin Shi, Wu Zhaoxuan, Smith, Fu Kai'er, and Feng Xike, with Wei Yifu as chairman. The meeting discussed the purchase of aircraft and resolved that two Junkers W33 aircraft, recently ordered, will be used for flights east of Xi'an. Due to the high mountains between Xi'an and Dihua, which make flying difficult, especially in the summer, it was decided to purchase three Junkers W43 aircraft, equipped with Hornet engines. (2) Regarding the salaries of personnel suspended from duty, it was resolved to revise and pass the interim method of granting consolation money to personnel suspended from duty, as drafted by Li Jingcong, Smith, and others. (A) Company personnel (excluding those dismissed for cause or those who resign voluntarily) shall be granted consolation money. However, this method does not apply when the company ceases operations or when contracts are in place. (B) The granting of consolation money shall be in accordance with the following regulations: For service of less than half a year, one-quarter of the monthly salary shall be granted; for service of half a year but less than one year, one-half of the monthly salary shall be granted; for service of one year, the full monthly salary shall be granted, and for each additional year of service, one-half of the monthly salary shall be added, but not to exceed three months. (C) The official salary of personnel suspended from duty shall be calculated on a daily basis. (D) This method shall be implemented from the date of approval by the Board of Directors. The meeting was adjourned.

Page 14

Rice Industry to Use New Standard Rice Measures

February 5th

The rice industry in this city has always used the Shenhu measure for transactions, which has been issued by the Renhu Association and used for decades. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau ordered the Bean and Rice Industry Association to switch to new measuring instruments as soon as possible and abolish the old Shenhu measure. It was originally scheduled to be implemented in January of last year, and the association had already manufactured more than 600 new measuring instruments with a capacity of eight dou and four sheng, and was informing various businesses to collect them. Unexpectedly, the war broke out in Shanghai, preventing the implementation. The association had submitted a request to the Social Affairs Bureau to postpone the implementation, and after repeated requests and reporting of various difficulties, it was delayed until now. Now that the measurement system has been reformed, the association has been ordered to notify its members to implement it immediately without further delay. The association recently convened a meeting of its members to decide on the date of implementation of the new measuring instruments and to calibrate the new measuring instruments before distributing them to various businesses. It was decided that the new measuring instruments would be implemented simultaneously by the northern and southern rice businesses on February 5th.

Establishment of General Management Office for Various Industries' Insurance

Chairman Wang Yansong... General Manager Fang Jiaobo

Leaders from various industries in the city, to promote Chinese business insurance and protect the interests of policyholders, have organized the General Management Office for Various Industries' Insurance Co., Ltd., located on the second floor of the Silk Industry Bank on Hankou Road. They act as agents for various insurance types, including marine, fire, life, accident, and automobile insurance. The company has been established, and Wang Yansong has been selected as chairman, Chen Songyuan, Chu Wenqi, and Lu Wenshao as executive directors, Fang Jiaobo as manager, and Ye Jiaxing and Bao Yudi as deputy managers. The official opening is scheduled for February 10th at 10:00 AM. Internal staff have been working since the 5th of this month. It is reported that many businesses have requested to become insurance agents recently, making the work very busy.

China Merchants Public Bus Company to Add Zhenru Express Bus

Since resuming operations, the Shanghai China Merchants Public Bus Company has been actively reorganizing transportation. Recognizing the large number of educators traveling to and from the Zhenru district, and the inconvenience of locals bringing baskets to the city on the same buses, causing crowding and frequent stops, the company has purchased several new vehicles and converted them into modern passenger buses with comfortable seating. These buses will travel directly from Shanghai to Zhenru without stopping along the way. They are currently being assembled day and night, and will be put into service as soon as they are completed. From then on, transportation to Zhenru will be even more convenient.

Memorial Service for Yu Zongzhou to Be Held Today

The memorial service for Pastor Yu Guozhen will be held at Yongzhi Hall on Xiangyin Road in northern Shanghai at 2:00 PM today. Mr. Zhang Zhijiang has been specially invited to preach. This afternoon, Xiangyin Road will likely be packed with people, making it a grand occasion.

Record of Meeting of Authors and Publishers

The Shanghai office of the Chinese Authors and Publishers Association convened a meeting of publishing organizations yesterday at Zhimei Restaurant on Fuzhou Road. Attendees included Hong Xuefan of the Modern Bookstore, Zhang Xishan of the Kaiming Bookstore, Li Zhiyun of the Beixin Bookstore, Zou Wenqing of the Shenzhou Guoguang Society, Tang Zhejun of the Huatong Bookstore, Wang Zicheng of the Guangming Bookstore, Wang Mengzou of the Yadong Library, Zhang Bingwen of the Pacific Bookstore, Ji Jianhua of the New China Bookstore, and over twenty others. Chairman Hong Xuefan first reported on the recent investigation of piracy by the association's secretary-general, Shi Zuocai, in the Northwest region, and the investigation in Taiyuan on the 23rd of last month with Yang, an inspector from the Beijing headquarters. Over 70 types of pirated books, totaling over 10,000 copies, were discovered at Fan Hua Company, Quan Ji, De Sheng Wen Huan, and other bookstores in the area. The shopkeepers were immediately arrested and taken to the public security bureau. The next day, they were tried, and the dishonest merchants were heavily fined. The pirated books were confiscated and destroyed. Shi originally planned to leave Beijing and continue investigating elsewhere, but after Fan Hua Company paid the fines and pledged to reform, they filed a counterclaim in the local court. Secretary-General Shi believes that although the company is backed by shareholder power, the evidence of their crime is solid, and he will not show weakness. He is determined to do his best to deal with them. In addition to requesting the Booksellers Association to send a telegram to the Shanxi court to uphold justice and punish the dishonest merchants according to the law, he is also planning other countermeasures. The meeting decided that the association should publish an advertisement in various port newspapers to warn pirate booksellers. Publishers who are members of the association should cease all dealings with any bookstore found selling pirated books. Li Zhiyun proposed that the association print a high-quality embossed copyright certificate to be affixed to the copyright page of each book, to make it easier to identify pirated books in various ports. The printing costs would be allocated among the members. This was unanimously approved. Finally, the chairman reported on his investigation of pirated books in Guangdong, Hong Kong, Shantou, and other places, and reported that the Commercial Press had nominated Li Bojia, head of the publishing department, to join the association, and on the collection of special donations for half a month. The meeting then adjourned.

Summary of the Annual Meeting of the Chinese Chemical Industry Association

The Chinese Chemical Industry Association believed that Hangzhou has shown great vigor in construction and higher education recently, and that the chemical industry is the foundation of all construction and national defense. Therefore, the 8th annual meeting was specially held in Hangzhou. Attendees included Xu Fengshi, Chen Pingcheng, Wang Jiliang, Cao Liangxia, Shen Xiongqing, He Shangping, Lin Jiyong, Li Shouheng, Yu Xueyang, Wu Zhitian, Gao Bojun, Wang Dong, Cheng Huanxi, Ji Yucheng, Shen Zhennan, Tang Yongjian, Wang Hanzeng, Wang Jicai, Shen Taogu, Bao Bodu, Gu Siqi, Pan Chengqi, Zhang Xiaoting, Xu Fengchao, Li Han, Cheng Enguang, Li Kunhou, Zhu Jingliang, Jin Peisong, Shao Jiajun, Wu Haoran, Chen Zhilin, Cheng Boshang, Dai Qixin, and over fifty others, who stayed at the West Lake Hotel. On New Year's Day, an administrative meeting was held at the Bank of China Villa, passing three resolutions: to promote association affairs, vigorously raise funds, and expand membership. Cao Liangxia and Wu Yunlu were elected as chairman and vice-chairman, Yu Xueyang and Shao Jialin as secretaries, Wang Jiliang as editor, Wang Zhudong as general affairs officer, Cheng Shixi as accountant, and Chen Pingcheng, Lin Jiyong, and He Shangping as councilors. At noon, the Hangzhou branch hosted a banquet at the Tianxiang Restaurant. In the evening, the association hosted a New Year's banquet at the YMCA. Zhou Yangchuan of the Minsheng Machinery Glass Factory, and representatives from Tianchu Monosodium Glutamate Factory, Wuzhou Pharmaceutical Factory, Family Industry Society, Chinese Chemical Industry Society, and Tihe Industrial Company provided gifts to add to the festivities. On the 2nd, the association invited the heads of the Construction Department and Education Department, the president of Zhejiang University, and Xu Fengshi and He Shangping to give public lectures at the YMCA. At noon, Lin Jiyong led students from the Fudan Chemistry Department to perform military chemical experiments at the public sports field. The program included liquid fire, bombs, aircraft incendiary bombs, smoke bombs, tear gas, and choking gas. Afterwards, the two departments hosted a public banquet at Jufeng Garden. In the afternoon, they visited the West Lake Condensed Milk Factory, the Minsheng Machinery Factory, the Minsheng Glass Factory, the Meilili Paper Factory, and the Zhejiang University College of Engineering. In the evening, Zhejiang University hosted a banquet. On the morning of the 3rd, the association held a presentation of papers at the College of Liberal Arts of Zhejiang University, with sixteen papers presented. In the afternoon, an industrial film was shown in the auditorium, featuring seven reels of the actual work of Hengxin Foreign Firm and Zhenhua Lacquer Company. In summary, the association held a grand propaganda meeting in Hangzhou at a time when our country's industry is backward and military affairs are strained, making the general public, who are immersed in pleasure and natural beauty, aware of the importance of the chemical industry for national defense and all aspects of clothing, food, housing, and transportation, hoping to awaken them to promote it. Therefore, its significance is very serious. However, it is a pity that newspapers were suspended, and news of the association was not published. This summary is specially presented, which is hoped to be what those who are interested in the chemical industry are concerned about.

News from Various Provincial Associations

The Shanghai Minnan Fellow Association held its 22nd board meeting yesterday, chaired by Qiu Hanping. It was resolved to send a telegram to the Ministry of Interior, urging Xiamen to be quickly established as an independent city. The original telegram is recorded below: To Song, Acting President of the Executive Yuan, and Huang, Minister of the Interior: Xiamen is one of the earliest trading ports in our country, guarding the throat of southern Fujian. Much of the trade with Southeast Asia starts here. Recently, many Fujianese have returned to the country, and investment has gradually increased. However, because Xiamen's municipal administration has historically been under the jurisdiction of the navy, management has been poor, and malpractices have been rampant, hindering its orderly development. The recent decision by the provincial government to change Xiamen into a city is in line with the wishes of the Fujianese people. We earnestly request that it be implemented quickly, and that the selection of the mayor be made carefully. We are eagerly anticipating this. Respectfully, the Shanghai Minnan Fellow Association.

The Shanghai Huining Fellow Association held a standing committee meeting on January 3rd to discuss various cases. (1) Regarding the holding of the association's 10th anniversary celebration and the 10th general membership recruitment, it was decided that the 10th recruitment would begin on February 9th and end on April 9th, followed by the opening of the 10th anniversary celebration and entertainment event. The detailed rules of procedure will be decided at a meeting of the various preparatory committees on the 8th of this month (Sunday). (2) Regarding the 10th election of the association, due to the postponement of the 9th election due to the war, it was postponed to June 1st. The term of office of the 9th committee is only half a year. Regarding whether to reschedule the election, it was decided to wait until after the end of the 10th general membership recruitment to determine the date of the election. The meeting then adjourned.

Inspection Report of Sze Ming Bank

The Sze Ming Bank's issuance reserve inspection report for December 31, 1932, states: The bank's issued banknotes have full reserves, with cash reserves of at least 60% and guarantee reserves of up to 40%. The inspection report by accountants Wu Zheng and Pan Zhaobang, and supervisors Xiang Fenglou and Zheng Xitang, is as follows: The total amount of exchange coupons issued is 15,094,600 yuan. The total amount of reserves is 15,094,600 yuan. This includes: The bank's issuance amount is 8,344,600 yuan, with cash reserves of 6,134,600 yuan and guarantees of 2,210,000 yuan. The amount used by fellow banks is 6,750,000 yuan, with cash reserves of 4,250,000 yuan and guarantees of 2,500,000 yuan.

Establishment of the Dried Goods Industry Union

The preparation of the Shanghai Dried Goods Industry Union has been completed. After applying for permission from the Party and government authorities, the inaugural meeting was held yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM in the auditorium of the General Labor Union in the city. More than 150 members attended. Chairman Yu Yaoqiu reported on the preparatory process. Subsequently, an election was held, and Zhu Bofeng, Cai Jiugao, Fei Zugen, Hu Ting, and eleven others were elected as directors, and Wang A Jin, Qian Liang, and five others were elected as supervisors. They were then sworn into office and nominated responsible persons to begin drafting improvements to labor-management conditions for submission to the Party and government authorities for mediation.

Talent Sought by the Vocational Guidance Office

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Office was entrusted yesterday by a certain organization in the city to hire a staff member who is proficient in both Chinese and English, skilled in translation, and has ample knowledge and experience in documentation (English typing skills are preferred). The monthly salary is approximately 60 yuan. Candidates should bring their work samples and contact the office every morning for interviews. Furthermore, a certain organization has commissioned the recruitment of investigators for the sugar industry, hardware industry, and tea industry, with those familiar with the content and business conditions of each industry being qualified. Those interested may visit the office at 80 Hualong Road for a personal interview. According to statistics released by the office for December of last year, 617 vocational consultations were conducted, 455 talents were registered, 53 business assignments were commissioned, and 34 individuals were successfully placed.

Long Mao's Postdated Checks Unredeemable Due to Bankruptcy, Lawsuit Filed

Long Mao Textile Company went bankrupt due to financial difficulties, owing more than one million yuan. It is currently being liquidated. The company issued a large number of postdated checks. Upon maturity, the company had already collapsed, and the holders of the checks were unable to redeem them, leading to lawsuits. The responsible parties of the company, Yang Xixian and Zhang Bingjun, have been repeatedly sued by creditors. Yang has fled to avoid punishment, and Zhang is also hiding in various places. Yesterday afternoon, during the summons by the First Special District Court, neither defendant appeared. Only Zhang's defense lawyer appeared in court, requesting a postponement. However, the lawyers for the plaintiffs Sun Zikui, Wang Baoyu, and Zhan Hongsen, Wu Linkun and Wang Fuchang, stated that the postdated checks held by the plaintiffs from Long Mao amounted to more than 100,000 taels of silver. To protect the interests of the plaintiffs, they had requested that the defendants be released on bail, but unfortunately it was not approved, allowing the defendant Yang Xixian to escape. Now, the second defendant, Zhang Bingjun, has also failed to appear. The lawyer's claim that Zhang has left Shanghai on business is unbelievable. Zhang even met with this lawyer this morning to discuss settlement issues. If he had the sincerity to settle, he could have surrendered to the authorities and requested a postponement to facilitate settlement. Instead, he falsely claimed to have left Shanghai, hoping to delay the matter. This clearly shows that he not only lacks the sincerity to settle, but also has the suspicion of deceiving the court. It is requested that a warrant be issued for his arrest to protect the interests of the plaintiffs. Judge Zhang then ordered a postponement until the 9th of this month to summon the defendant for further questioning.

Schoolboy Shot Dead with Hunting Rifle

Zhang Guosheng Suspected and Accused

Wang Genxing Dies Tragically for No Reason

Wang Changchun, a farmer in Dongwei, Ershisi Tu, Dongnan Yuanbei City, Tangqiao, Pudong, is over fifty years old and has only one son (the only son in Wang's fourth branch), named Genxing, who is ten years old. He cherishes him like a treasure. He is currently studying at Dongxiang Yaojing Elementary School. Unexpectedly, at around 4:00 PM on November 23rd of the lunar calendar, Genxing was returning home from school and, while passing the intersection of Nanqing Village, was suddenly struck in the left temple by a stray bullet. The bullet did not pass through, and he fell to the ground and died on the spot. At the time, Genxing's classmates Wang Xirong and Wang Xigen were walking with him and witnessed a person wearing a Western suit, holding a long gun, and carrying a yellow armadillo. After the incident, he ran away frantically. Wang Xirong and others immediately reported to Wang Changchun, who arrived and mourned over the body. He reported the information to the township office, which forwarded it to the district office, and requested officials to be sent to examine the body, put it in a coffin, and await the arrest of the perpetrator and the investigation of punishment. Wang Changchun is now suffering from unbearable grief over the tragic death of his only son. After investigating and confirming the surname of the murderer, he filed a complaint with the authorities the day before yesterday, stating that his son Genxing was actually killed by Zhang Guosheng, who lived in Xitang, Yaotu. This has been proven by Wang Rong and Wang Xigen. (According to the complaint, Zhang Guosheng is the only person in a Western suit in this village.) It is said that there were no other hunters on that day, and that the defendant Zhang Guosheng often carries a gun to hunt birds and animals, and keeps a hunting dog, which is well known in the village. After the defendant caused the incident, he fled without a trace and instructed his uncle, Zhang Xiaodi, to hand over the long gun and scattered beads to the security regiment as a way to deny the crime, which actually serves as proof. Now, he is still at large, which is truly unbearable. If he is not arrested and investigated, how can the injustice be avenged? Therefore, he requests that the defendant Zhang Guosheng be strictly arrested, punished according to the law, and that the law be upheld. It is ordered that we wait for a thorough investigation.

Shop Owner Punished for Bribing Guarantor

The Fuli Hat Factory at No. 339 Yuezhou Road, previously submitted a statement to the First Special District Court guaranteeing the case of the defendant Tang Zaiheng. Following routine procedure, the court dispatched translator Chen Shidi along with police officers in a court vehicle to the Fuli Hat Factory to investigate whether it was a reputable business to determine whether to approve or reject the guarantee. The manager of Fuli, Yuan Shixun, fearing that the investigation would reveal that the business was not qualified to be a guarantor, ordered his son, Yuan Shanfu, to instruct shop employees Zhang Quantai and Xu Shouchang to intercede with Chen and others, and offer them four dollars as a gift, claiming it was a small amount to cover transportation costs. This behavior was clearly bribery to deceive people. Chen Shidi immediately presented the money to Court President Guo Yun'guan and reported the bribery by Yuan and others truthfully. President Guo was shocked and angry. In addition to issuing a notice strictly prohibiting litigants from bribing public officials, or public officials from soliciting all kinds of illegal fees, and allowing reports to be filed and investigated according to the law, Prosecutor Zhang of the court's prosecutor's office issued a warrant to summon Yuan and his son, Zhang Quantai, Xu Shouchang, and others to investigate. At the conclusion of the investigation, it was determined that the evidence of bribery of public officials by these individuals was conclusive and unforgivable. Therefore, a public prosecution was filed in the corresponding criminal court. Judge Zhang Junqing opened the court for a clear hearing. Yesterday afternoon was the day for the verdict. Yuan and the other four defendants and their defense lawyers did not appear. Judge Zhang then announced the verdict: Yuan Shixun, Yuan Shanfu, Zhang Quantai, and Xu Shouchang were each sentenced to two months in prison for bribing public officials, and the four dollars of bribery money was confiscated. This severe punishment should serve as a warning to others.

Banning the "Strange Hero Zhang Jiuguan" Play

丨Characters in the play are taken from lotteries, must be changed丨

丨Newly compiled scripts must be applied for according to law丨

The "Strange Hero Zhang Jiuguan" play performed by the Qitian Stage not only involves gods and monsters, but also takes character names such as Cheng Tianlong, Chen Fengchun, Li Mingqiu, Fang Maolin, Chen Rongsheng, and Chen Pangui from lotteries. The Municipal Education Bureau believes that the harm of lotteries to the people is no different from a flood or a wild beast, and is known to all. Taking names from lotteries for the play is akin to promoting them, which violates the prohibition. The stage was ordered to remove the parts about gods and monsters, and to change all the character names taken from lotteries. It has now been heard that the Municipal Education Bureau has ordered the Actors' Union to notify them that they have not complied. If they continue to ignore the orders, they will be strictly banned. A script application form was attached and forwarded to each stage. In the future, each stage is instructed to pay attention to newly compiled scripts and to apply for review according to the law.

Dual Assault Leads to Litigation

≡Noodle Bowl and Wine Bottle Used as Weapons≡

≡Both Defendants Receive Suspended Sentences of Detention≡

Li Qiu-ding, a Korean woman residing at No. 35, Lao Guan Li, Jiaxing Road, went out to buy noodles around 1 a.m. on the 23rd of last month. Upon returning to her doorstep, she was accosted by Zhang Jin-de from Yancheng, Chen Si-quan from Anhui, and Cha Zheng-fa, all heavily intoxicated. Mistaking her for a prostitute, they began teasing her. Li, speaking in Japanese, cursed at them. Zhang and the others continued to follow her, leading to mutual insults. Li, greatly angered, threw the noodles she was carrying at them. Zhang and the others, equally enraged, started fighting. Her husband, Zhao Bing-xuan, a Korean man, hearing the commotion, came outside and struck Zhang Jin-de on the head with a wine bottle, knocking him to the ground. Li also sustained minor injuries to her back and abdomen. The Hongkou Concession police, both Chinese and foreign, arrived after being alerted and arrested the three men, taking them to the police station. They were later sent to the First Special District Court. Zhang Tian-yin, the police lawyer, recounted the events, stating that the victim, Li Qiu-ding, was eight months pregnant and, after suffering injuries to her abdomen, was admitted to Fumin Hospital at No. 412, North Sichuan Road. Doctors found that the fetus had stopped breathing, posing a serious danger. She recovered after several days of treatment. The defendants claimed at the police station that Li was actually a prostitute and that they intended to go inside to have fun. However, investigations revealed that the house where Li lived had indeed been a brothel in the past. Li Qiu-ding then explained her version of events, accusing all three defendants of assaulting her. Her husband, Zhao Bing-xuan, testified that he owned a ginseng shop at a certain address on Ximen Road in the French Concession, leaving early and returning late. On the day in question, his wife Li Qiu-ding went out to buy groceries and was harassed by the three defendants. He used a wine bottle to injure the first defendant's head. Zhang Jin-de and the others insisted that the plaintiff was a prostitute. They claimed that they were drunk and went inside to solicit services, seeing many women there. After agreeing on a price for the night, two Korean men attacked them with a stove and iron tools, causing injuries. They denied hitting Li Qiu-ding. As the testimonies differed, Judge Zhao ordered them to be remanded in custody pending judgment. Yesterday morning, at the Third Criminal Court, Zhang Jin-de, Chen Si-quan, and Cha Zheng-fa were each sentenced to fifty days of detention, with a three-year suspended sentence.

Three Boat Collision Accidents in One Day

Yesterday, three boat collision accidents occurred, all reported to the Water Police Station for record. They are listed below: (1) Yesterday at 11:00 a.m., Sun Lan-yin's brick boat, carrying 18,000 bricks, was sailing north from the Nanosaka Pier. Suddenly, an empty pig boat, also sailing north with the current, collided with the brick boat's portside midship, causing damage but luckily not capsizing. (2) Yesterday at 1:50 p.m., the Meifu No. 5 tugboat, towing a pier boat, was sailing upstream from Yangshupu when a stone sailboat sailing south suddenly collided with the tugboat's bow near the Lujiazui area, causing significant damage to both vessels. (3) Yesterday at 2:30 p.m., the Pujiang No. 5 "Baixiang" boat was docked at Lujiazui when, during low tide, Zhou De-jue's pottery boat also drifted to the same spot and accidentally collided with the "Baixiang" boat's stern, shattering the side timbers.

Page 15

First Special Court Hears Bribery Case Against Sanyou Factory Bosses Yesterday

Court Orders Rehearing 丨丨丨

The labor dispute at the Sanyou Industrial Company in Yinxiang Port, Pudong, has led to the company officials bribing the standing director of the Seventh District Cotton Textile Workers' Union, Gong Yuting, to halt labor union activities. Gong subsequently handed over the 200 yuan bribe, along with a report on the incident to the labor union and Bureau of Social Affairs. The labor union, alleging that the company officials had publicly committed bribery in violation of criminal statutes, retained lawyer Wei Wenhan to file charges with the First Special District Court. The court granted the request and summoned a fifth criminal court hearing to be held on December 27th of last year. Due to the defendant, Shen Jiucheng, failing to appear, the official ordered a rescheduling of the hearing. The following is a detailed record of yesterday’s continuing trial.

The Opening of the Trial

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00, judge Liu Yugui, accompanied by court clerk Huang Haiyun, was seated in the fifth criminal court to begin the hearing. The plaintiff's representatives, Zhang Wenhai and Gong Zishen, defense lawyer Wei Wenhan, defendants Shen Jiucheng, Wang Xianhua, Chen Wanyun, Cen Zihou, Lao Huimin, Li Daofa, defense lawyers Tan Yigong and Yu Zhongluo, and witness Gong Yuting, all appeared on time. The judge began by questioning the defendant, Shen Jiucheng, who testified that he had indeed relinquished his duties at the Sanyou Industrial Company on November 25th of last year. He explained that he had been unable to attend the previous hearing due to illness in Hangzhou and was now appearing in court despite being ill.

Witness Testimony

Witness Gong Yuting then testified that the Sanyou Company had not sought a legitimate resolution to the labor dispute and instead sent representatives Li Daofa and Lao Huimin to collude with worker Xia Zhongzhao, instructing him to meet with Gong at the Great World Entertainment Center in early November of last year. Later, they met at the Oriental Hotel. Gong, believing that there was no harm in meeting as the dispute had not been fully resolved, agreed to attend. However, the discussions resulted in no agreement and the meeting ended without resolution. At the end of the same month, Xia Zhongzhao notified Gong, instructing him to meet at the Great Southern Restaurant. Gong refused. On December 3rd of the same year, Xia Zhongzhao said, "The company has instructed me to give you one hundred yuan for your use. You just need to give me a receipt." Gong refused. On the 6th of that month, Xia Zhongzhao notified Gong to meet with the defendants, Lao Huimin and others, in a room surnamed Chen in room 228 of the Zhongzhou Hotel. Gong agreed to attend. At the meeting, Gong found Lao Huimin, Li Daofa, Xia Zhonghai, Xia Zhongzhao, and Zheng Xiangrong present. Lao Huimin then stated that the company was willing to pay Xia Zhongzhao and Gong two thousand yuan, and other responsible parties one thousand yuan. The only requirement was that Gong and Xia cease union activities and allow the members to resolve the dispute on their own accord. Gong reluctantly agreed. Following the meeting, Gong immediately reported the incident to the union and submitted the bribe money to the Bureau of Social Affairs. A receipt was provided as evidence.

Rehearing Ordered

The court ordered that, as the details of the case required further investigation, and Xia Zhongzhao needed to be summoned for questioning, the hearing would be rescheduled for 2:00 p.m. on the 11th of this month. At that time, many factory workers were listening to the trial in the gallery. The defendant's defense lawyer, fearing that the workers would surround the court, requested that the court prevent such action. The court advised the listening workers to await the lawful resolution of the labor dispute and refrain from any unproductive actions that might violate the law. The court then ordered the workers to leave first.

Continued Hearing of the Estate Dispute of the Late Tycoon Qiu Weiqing

≡Sixty-Year-Old Concubine Faces Off Against Adopted Son in Court≡

Following the death of the late paint tycoon Qiu Weiqing, his adopted son, Changsheng, was sued in the First Special District Court by his concubine, Sun, and his sister, Zhu Qiu (Weiqing's biological sister), on the grounds of attempting to seize the inheritance and failing to provide for the safe upbringing of his underage biological children, Changyin, and others. The circumstances of the hearing at the end of last year were reported in this newspaper. Yesterday (the 7th) afternoon, the court's Judge Qian reopened the case in the Second Tribunal. First, the plaintiff's legal representative, Zhang Shizhao, stated that he was requesting the dismissal of the second defendant, Chang Shuliu, and the third defendant, Ren Yian, as it had been verified that everything was initiated by the first defendant, Qiu Changsheng, and they did not wish to cause further complications. Qiu Sun, with assistance, stood in the plaintiff's column. Zhu Qiu, who was ill and unable to attend, stated the intent of the lawsuit. Due to deafness making it difficult to respond, the representative, lawyer Zhang Shizhao, stood up to state that the first plaintiff, Sun, was the concubine of the late Qiu Weiqing, and the second plaintiff, Zhu Qiu, was Weiqing's sister. Before Weiqing's death, he arranged for Shuying, the daughter of his concubine Jia, and his son Changyin to be adopted into Sun's name to be raised by her. Furthermore, due to the adoption by his legal wife, Zhou,

Changsheng, the Adopted Son

had reached adulthood. Fearing that his biological children were weak and vulnerable and would be subject to abuse by relatives, he specifically stipulated in his will while ill that all property should be managed by his nephew, Sheng-san, until his biological children reached adulthood, at which point Changyin and others would be allowed to inherit. However, in January of 1925, Weiqing passed away, and Changsheng immediately took back all the inheritance from Sheng-san and divided it. Changsheng, as an adopted son, seized forty to fifty percent of the inheritance, while five to fifty percent was placed under the name of his biological child, Changyin, disregarding his stepdaughter Shuying. Relatives were neither named nor

consulted about this illegal division of property.

Sun, unable to bear witness to it, went to Hangzhou for medical treatment. Both biological children were cared for by their biological mother, Jia, so there were no concerns. However, on March 4th of last year, Jia also passed away due to illness. The defendant, Changsheng, immediately seized the opportunity, forcibly opening the locked safe with the intent to steal the inheritance. Fellow villagers, feeling indignant, reported the incident to the police, who then sent officers to guard the safe for more than ten days. In addition, he argued that even the residence on Tongfu Road was not a husband acting like a real man but rather a woman making accusations.

Money is the Root of All Evil and Causes One to Be Bullied

"Pockmarked" Liu Hangs Himself in Anger

Liu Wenbing, known as "Pockmarked," of Jingjiang, currently residing at No. 395 Dongyangjiazhai, Lan Nidu North, Pudong, worked at the Xiaoshedud ferry plant. Due to owing a debt to a fellow villager, Cao, of No. 208 Hutang Street, the latter came to Liu to demand payment. As Liu was unable to pay, Cao slapped Liu several times. Liu, as a man, felt ashamed to be slapped by a woman. In such circumstances, money was the only cause. In a moment of anger, he secretly hanged himself at home in the afternoon. Liu only had one sister, Liu Abao, who lived with him. When she returned home and discovered the suicide, it was too late to save him. She reported the incident to the Third District Police Department, who detained Cao. Yesterday, police officer Xie Along reported the incident to the local court. Prosecutor Zhang and others were dispatched to the scene for investigation. After confirming the death, they ordered the family to prepare the body for burial and await further instructions.

The biological child Changyin was supposed to be in the possession of, was also seized by Changsheng. The security measures Jia had employed during her lifetime to prevent Changsheng from harming her son were extremely strict, with the house divided into sections separated by electric fences. Now, the defendant has taken advantage of the deaths of Weiqing and Jia, one after the other

stealing the property and lives of the orphans

and placing them under his control. He calls it the "Organization of Management Committee," but in reality, it is to isolate Changyin and others from their relatives so that he can carry out his malicious plan of infringement. Therefore, the first plaintiff, as the adoptive mother, and the second plaintiff, as the aunt by blood relation, are both unable to participate in the upbringing of the two orphans, and the defendant Changsheng's premeditated infringement is clearly evident with existing evidence. Therefore, they jointly file a lawsuit, requesting legal punishment. The defendant's defense lawyer stated that the plaintiff, Qiu Sun, had signed an agreement severing ties with the Qiu family and thus had no right to sue. The second plaintiff had no familial relationship with Jia and thus could not file a lawsuit under the relevant self-prosecution laws. The lawyer argued that the case should first be dismissed on procedural grounds. The plaintiff's lawyer, Zheng Wenkai, argued that whether the separation agreement was valid or not, since it was obtained through

deception and fraud

was a matter of civil law and had no relevance to the case. Furthermore, Sun, being sixty years old, would never sever her family ties with her adopted son after her husband's death, so Sun herself was one of the victims, as had already been stated in her complaint. As for Zhu Qiu, after the death of her brother, his will was violated, and his property was seized. As for the orphans, a meeting of relatives was not legally convened to jointly fulfill the responsibility of guardianship. Therefore, her personal legal rights had also been clearly infringed upon, and she had the right to seek redress, the lawyer stated. Judge Qian then stated that there was no need for either side to argue further about procedural law, as the court would proceed according to law. Having

legal basis

But Changyin and others have always been raised by Sun, which is not difficult to see from the separation contract. The defendant should try to reconcile outside the court in accordance with humanity and law. In accordance with the law, the self-prosecution case should be withdrawn by the self-prosecutor, and the procurator's consent should be sought. In a case that applies to public prosecution or self-prosecution, the original hearing allows the parties to choose on their own, and there is no big difference. Since this case is a family issue, it is best for both parties to negotiate and reconcile, otherwise each should do their best to provide evidence in order to conclude the case quickly. The self-prosecuting attorney requested bail because the defendant had failed to appear at the previous protest, and was ordered to be released by attorney Wang, with an order to be present whenever summoned.

After Swallowing Opium and Red Pills, He Knew He Would Die and Cried Aloud in Bed

Suicide with a Difficult-to-Express Secret

Pan Xiangfu is Truly Pitiful

At the Qianjixian Inn, located in front of the Nanchezhan Road District Court, a man checked in the day before yesterday, registering as Pan Xiangfu, 32 years old, a local resident from Chenjiaqiao in front of the South Railway Station. He worked as a lineman at the China Merchants Electric Company. He booked room number eight and stayed for two days, appearing depressed and deeply troubled. The tea server paid attention. Yesterday at 11:30 AM, this person suddenly cried loudly in bed. The tea server inquired, but he initially refused to speak. Seeing a note on the table addressed to Xu Jinfu in the repair line department of China Merchants Electric Company, he realized it was a suicide attempt. After repeated questioning, he confessed to smoking two small opium bubbles and swallowing two red pills, knowing he was about to die, hence his sorrow. When asked why he was committing suicide, he firmly refused to say, stating it was a difficult-to-express secret that outsiders should not know. The tea server reported to the police, who sent him to the Second District Police Station, then to Shanghai Hospital for treatment, but it is unknown if his life can be saved.

Repeatedly Chopped with Fourteen Axes

Wang Maosheng's Life is in Peril

Nasal Septum Split Open, Assailant Escapes

At approximately 9 PM last night, Wang Maosheng Lumber Mill on Jiaozhou Road in Western Shanghai employed Wang Aimei, a 44-year-old man from Haizhou, as a night watchman. While patrolling the mill, three strangers arrived and, without explanation, attacked Wang with axes. He was struck seven times on the head, three times on the left arm, and twice on the left hand and right arm. His face, particularly his nasal septum, was severely lacerated. He fell to the ground in a pool of blood. Wang cried out loudly for help, startling the assailants, who fled. Passersby heard the commotion and alerted the police, who arrived and transported Wang to Baolong Hospital for treatment. His injuries are reported to be critical, and his life is in danger.

Hu Shengfang Steals Goods... Attempted Murder... Throws into the River

Boatman Rescues Four Lives, Truth Comes to Light

Ren Xinghui, a 21-year-old from Pinghu residing on Huade Road in the northern part of the city, had an acquaintance named Hu Shengfang from Changzhou. Several days prior, Hu stole clothing and other items belonging to Ren's cousin, Li Hongsheng, worth over one hundred yuan, and fled with the loot. Li and Ren searched diligently. Yesterday around 5 PM, Ren encountered Hu, and demanded the return of the stolen items. Hu replied that he had already pawned everything. "If you want the money, you can come with me to Pudong to get it," Hu said. Ren, believing him, followed Hu to the Ningshao Wharf at the Dongmen Road intersection in the South City, intending to hire a boat to cross to Pudong. Unexpectedly, Hu suddenly pushed Ren into the river. A passing boatman saw him fall and quickly steered his boat over to rescue him. Ren was saved from drowning. Seeing Ren being rescued, Hu, realizing that Ren would not let the matter rest and would likely turn him in, panicked and decided to commit suicide. Seeing the rushing river before him, he jumped in. The boatman, having just rescued one person from the river, was astonished to see another person jump from the wharf. He rescued Hu as well. The boatman handed both men over to Officer Chen Rongji, who brought them to the First District Police Station. After a preliminary investigation by the district chief, he ordered a formal report and interrogation.

A Shot Rings Out in the Bathhouse

Around 7 PM the night before last, two thugs entered a bathhouse on Nanmatou in the First District of the South City and argued with a patron, Jin. Without warning, one of the thugs drew a pistol and fired at Jin. The bullet grazed Jin's left side and struck the cement floor, creating a hole. Jin stood frozen in shock while the thugs fled. Nearby police officers heard the shot and investigated, but everyone inside the bathhouse remained silent, and no one dared to testify. The First District sent senior officers to investigate, but they only found the bullet mark. The investigation is ongoing.

Rickshaw Puller Finds Abandoned Gun

Zhong Lihuai, a native of Jiangbei, supports himself by pulling a rickshaw. Around 2 PM the day before yesterday, Zhong was waiting for customers at the intersection of Malan Road and Pubai Road in the French Concession. A man, around 20 years old, wearing a green short shirt and trousers, jumped into his rickshaw, urgently ordering Zhong to pull quickly. Zhong immediately set off at a brisk pace. Suddenly, several people came chasing after them, and a police whistle sounded behind them. The man secretly placed a pistol in Zhong's rickshaw without him noticing, jumped out of the rickshaw, and fled. Zhong, seeing the man's hurried arrival and sudden departure, was bewildered. He could only accept his bad luck. In the evening, Zhong returned to the rickshaw lodging at No. 15 Huining Road outside the Dananmen in the South City to return the rickshaw. While cleaning the carriage, he lifted the carriage lid and was shocked to find a pistol. He immediately reported it to the lodging owner, Yu Dajin, who reported the incident to the Third Substation of the First District. Director Jin determined that the gun was a 4-inch Browning pistol, number 98285, with five bullets still in the chamber. Due to the nature of firearms, he ordered a report to be submitted to the Shanghai Public Safety Bureau for verification.

Reader's Forum

"Who is the Creator of Evil?"

| Message from Mr. Wang Lide

Reference to this column, December 29th

The question raised by Mr. Wu Jiaying in your newspaper on December 29th is: "Who is the creator of evil?" The intention is to explain that in the tragedy of social interaction between dancing girls and dance patrons in Shanghai dance halls, the protagonist is the dancing girl, because she is the initiator, while the man is passive. Therefore, he confidently states: "Clearly, the initiator is the plaintiff, while the passive party is accused of rape. Individual crime is established here, and the creation of social degradation also lies here." In reality, this is probably Mr. Wu's subjective view. We must ask, what is the purpose of today's urban dance halls? What need do they meet? Frankly speaking, today's dance halls are disguised prostitution, and not the "Changsan" (high-class courtesan) type of prostitution, but the "Yaoer" (second-class courtesan) type, even the street prostitutes on the main roads. The lower class is equivalent to the "wild chickens" of Sima Road and Beijing Road. In today's industrialized cities or commercial ports where goods are produced, the majority of women naturally cannot escape the consequence of rationalized production—the general rule of overpopulation. They cannot find work and become unemployed, so they naturally become prostitutes, simply transforming their labor to provide spiritual exploitation for the wealthy. Dancing girls are a higher form of this type of unemployed woman selling her labor in this way. When dancing girls dance with people, it is not the mutual enjoyment of dancing between two sexes in an ordinary social setting. She is subject to the free choice of the dance patron; she does not have the freedom to choose which guest she dances with. This is the same as serving customers in a "tangzi" (brothel) or responding to a "jupiao" (call slip). Therefore, unless there is an actual act of crime and a dancing girl is accused of rape by the plaintiff on the spot, we cannot consider the dancing girl to have been raped, because in reality, she not only provides entertainment through dancing but also inevitably tends to satisfy people's desires with her body, and this is a universal fact. However, if the dance patron uses this argument to defend his innocence, then he is wrong. Since we acknowledge that the dance hall is a place of prostitution, then if you go to a place of prostitution, you originally intended to flirt with the dancing girl. "Once you enter a place of right and wrong, you will become a person of right and wrong." Since you have entered a place of right and wrong, you are there to seek trouble. How can you place the blame entirely on the dancing girl? That is somewhat unfair. I want to say something fair: dancing girls and dance patrons are "half a pound and eight ounces" (equal). It is true that dancing girls often make unreasonable accusations or have to meet in court because they are abandoned halfway or because the dance patron has some money and they take the opportunity to extort money. All in all, the damnable private property system harms people. They are constantly influenced and encouraged to commit such crimes. Among the dance patrons, there are many "chai ba dang" (confidence tricksters) who specialize in sleeping with dancing girls. Of course, there are also some young masters who are cheated by them, but to say that men are entirely passive is unfair and not factual. Therefore, the open debauchery of dancing girls and dance patrons is an inevitable phenomenon in today's urban society. In that case, today's urban society is the creator of this evil. Then we ask: What is the result of today's urban society? It is formed by the method of production and relations of production under the current private property system. The day that we trace the origin, the so-called "creator of evil" mentioned by Mr. Wu is the aforementioned social relations of production. When we observe today's dance halls from the perspective of our materialistic sociology, it is truly a place of crime. If we want to find a way to "eliminate this cause," then on the one hand, everyone must rise up to do the work of "removing the root and blocking the source" and transform this breeding ground for evil. On the other hand, everyone should promote legitimate forms of entertainment as much as possible or encourage young people to study and reduce the opportunity for young people to be in dance halls. This is one aspect. On the one hand, from the social perspective, do everything possible to find work for women so that the majority of them have legitimate jobs. On the other hand, let them equally enjoy legitimate social interaction and legitimate entertainment, and equally encourage them to read and study, and increase their upward aspirations. Who would want to do this "civilized flesh business?" This is the second aspect. However, if the work of "removing the root and blocking the source" is not accelerated, then the latter two methods are only "treating the head when it hurts, and treating the feet when they hurt," and their effectiveness is visible. Understanding this point, then questions such as "Will Shanghai have fewer crimes if there are no dance halls? Will Shanghai have fewer shortcomings if there are no dance halls?" will be easily solved. Because Shanghai's dance halls are the product of Shanghai society; but the shortcomings of Shanghai society are not the product of Shanghai dance halls.

Southwest Political Affairs Committee Education Reform Committee Announces Outline for Education System Reform

Abolish Winter and Summer Vacations, Divide School Year into Four Semesters

Shorten Study Periods for Elementary, Secondary, and Higher Education

Committee Chairman Zou Lu Expresses Views

Guangzhou, 7th, Reuters Telegram - The Southwest Political Affairs Committee's Education Reform Committee announced the following outline for education system reform: (1) Abolish the winter and summer vacation system. (2) Shorten the length of study to five years for primary education, five years for secondary education, and three years for higher education. (3) Divide the school year into four semesters: the first semester from July to September, the second semester from October to December, the third semester from January to March, and the fourth semester from April to June. (4) Have a one-week break at the end of each semester.

▲Zou Lu Expresses Views: Zou Lu, chairman of the Education Reform Committee and president of National Sun Yat-sen University, expressed his views, stating that winter and summer vacations are merely habits and have no special reason. If it is said to be due to severe cold and heat, then Sweden and Norway should study for half a year and rest for half a year, and it should be impossible to establish schools in Nanyang and Africa, but this is not the case in reality. Moreover, most of China is in the temperate zone and does not have severe cold or heat, so this issue should not arise. If it is said to be for the purpose of mental and physical recuperation, then society is not limited to scholars, so why do farmers, workers, and merchants not have winter and summer vacations? Even if scholars are engaged in mental labor, there are more than just scholars in society who engage in mental labor. Moreover, after the abolition of winter and summer vacations, in addition to weekly holidays, there are still seven days at the end of each semester, which is more rest than that of farmers, workers, merchants, and other social service workers engaged in mental labor. Moreover, studying is like sailing against the current; if you do not advance, you will retreat. If you expose yourself to it for a few days and then freeze yourself for a few days, how much can you achieve? Based on these reasons, it is advocated to abolish winter and summer vacations and to shorten the school year, namely five years for primary education, five years for secondary education, and three years for higher education. Because with winter and summer vacations, primary and secondary schools only study for forty weeks each year, totaling two hundred and forty weeks for six years, and universities only study for thirty-six weeks each year, totaling one hundred and forty-four weeks for four years. If winter and summer vacations are abolished, primary and secondary schools can study for forty-eight weeks each year, totaling two hundred and forty weeks for five years, and universities can study for forty-eight weeks each year, totaling one hundred and forty-four weeks for three years. If this is the case, the study time is the same, but the graduation time is greatly reduced. (1) It is beneficial to national finances, (2) It is beneficial to the national economy, (3) Education is easier to popularize, and (4) Talents are easier to cultivate widely. During this time of national crisis, the people should intensify their work, which is especially necessary. However, for this system to be implemented, it is necessary to increase teachers' salaries in order to provide teachers with savings or retirement funds. Vacation rules for teachers should also be implemented so that after several years of teaching, they can have one year of vacation to increase their knowledge and recuperate their bodies and minds.

Special Appeal to College and High School Students Nationwide to Practice Education to Save the Nation (11) You Huai Gao

(12) How College Students Should Begin Work

1. Every college student and one high school student, or two high school students, form an education to save the nation group, named the [Province] [County] [District] [Village] Number [Number] Education to Save the Nation Group.

2. They must be assigned by the "[County] Education to Save the Nation Association" before being assigned to work in a certain village.

3. They must implement their work under the guidance of the "Education to Save the Nation Association," but they have the right to suggest methods.

4. After arriving in the countryside, they must consult with members of the local "[District] Education to Save the Nation Advancement Association" to discuss and arrange matters.

5. Select a suitable civilian residence to establish a school, but do not use forceful means to occupy it.

6. Clean up the doors, windows, roof, walls, and ground of the house. Repair what needs to be repaired, and paint what needs to be painted. The association will guide the methods.

7. Arrange the playground.

8. The association will allocate all expenses and equipment related to desks, chairs, paintings, teaching materials, paper, pens, as well as bedroom, kitchen, and toilet supplies.

9. Convene a meeting of villagers.

10. Prepare teaching materials.

11. Recruit students to enroll in school.

12. Implement education under the guidance of the association.

13. Conduct surveys under the guidance of the association.

14. Implement military training under the guidance of the association.

15. Implement other work under the guidance of the association: (1) Organize cooperatives, (2) Organize agricultural improvement societies, (3) Organize machinery engineering offices, (4) Organize medical and pharmaceutical societies, (5) Organize rural clubs.

(13) The Duties of the Education to Save the Nation Association

The Education to Save the Nation Association in each university and high school can be called the [School] Education to Save the Nation Association, which is similar to the previous student associations in each school. Because teachers and staff can be invited to participate together, this organization is the source of the cause of saving the nation and the organization that produces teachers. Therefore, after implementation, it will become a kind of preparation and examination organization. Therefore, every college and high school student must study education and research education in school during their studies, and during vacations, they can go to the village of their classmates or to their own village to conduct investigations and internships to prepare for their work after graduation. There is another extremely important matter, that is, every Education to Save the Nation Association is a very thorough examination organization, examining the achievements and behavior of each student in the village. These are the two responsibilities of the Education to Save the Nation Association in each school. The Education to Save the Nation Associations in each school can organize the [Province] Education to Save the Nation Association in a province, and then the Education to Save the Nation Associations in each province can organize the National Education to Save the Nation Association, but there must be absolutely no political role, so that the true meaning of saving the nation will not be lost, because saving the nation is an external matter, not an internal matter. There is also an Education to Save the Nation Association, which uses the county as a unit, and its name can be called the [Province] [County] Education to Save the Nation Association, which is organized by teachers from all villages in the county and convened and organized by the county magistrate. It is a formal organization and is subordinate to the Education to Save the Nation Association in each province, district, and city. Therefore, this County Education to Save the Nation Association also has two responsibilities, that is, connecting the Association above and connecting the villages below.

Finally, Chen Defu, representative of the school's alumni association, and Luo Guangrong, student representative, delivered congratulatory speeches, and the ceremony concluded. To celebrate the completion of the school building, a results exhibition and a fun fair were held on the 1st and 2nd. Many people visited the results exhibition and praised the efforts of the school's faculty and students after the war. The fun fair on the 1st and 2nd nights featured more than 30 different programs, with a total audience of more than 5,000 people. This was not only an unprecedented event for the school but also marked a new era of entertainment in Zhabei after the war. Residents of Zhabei were all overjoyed. The school was originally scheduled to hold a sports meet on the 1st, but due to the muddy ground, the school affairs committee decided to postpone it until the spring of next year.

Since the Girls' Department of Huadong Middle School, located on Belle Road and Xujiahui Road in the French Concession, was approved for registration by the City Education Bureau, school affairs have been progressing rapidly.
