Movie Special

Sunday, January 8th, 2023 (No extra charge)

Movie News

The Success Story of Underwater Photography

— Sheng Zhanneng

Movies value novelty, and the "novelty" is what photography technicians consider carefully. For example, Williamson didn't know how much effort he put in before the film "Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea" was made.

Usually, if you want to photograph underwater scenes, you usually store water in a glass tank in the photography field and arrange underwater scenes in the water for shooting. But this kind of photography cannot get the truth of the seabed. The young photographer Ernest Williamson felt this and studied hard. As a result, the ideal became a reality and he finally achieved the ideal of directly photographing the seabed.

Williamson's father, Charlie Williamson, was a famous underwater pipe inventor. Williamson and his younger brother George worked together to improve the underwater pipe invented by their father, making it a freely retractable pipe with large glass installed at the end of the pipe. The mother ship sank the pipe to the bottom of the sea, allowing it to freely photograph on the seabed.

When preparations were complete, the Williamson brothers sank the pipe to the bottom of the sea, ready to photograph. However, because the seabed was too dark, they also sank an electric light that could emit strong light. As a result of sinking the electric light, not only was the seabed bright enough to be photographed, but the fish on the seabed also gathered in all directions when they saw the electric light, resulting in better photos. Thus, the world's first underwater photography was announced successful on June 18, 1913.

Underwater photography is not possible everywhere. It is best to choose a sandy seabed. Also, because of the relationship between the tide and the mother ship's air supply, and because the technicians cannot stay underwater for too long, it takes a long time to shoot an underwater film. Williamson went through extraordinary hard work and effort, and finally made a film titled "Williamson's Underwater Adventure."

Universal Film Company saw this film and greatly appreciated it. Thinking that just shooting underwater scenes was not interesting enough, they had to create a fantasy to make the underwater scenes unfold before the audience to increase interest. So they hired Mr. Williamson to start filming "Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea." As soon as this film came out, all the secrets of the seabed were active in our eyes, and our horizons expanded a lot, and we added infinite surprise and magnificent feelings.

Bing Crosby and His Dog

Bing Crosby is the biggest radio star of today. He met us in "The Big Broadcast." His dog, of course, is also not ordinary.

New Year Movie Review

Several Premiere Films

— Yan Nan

This year's New Year's Day, nine theaters are showing first-run films. Movie fans are really lucky. Now I will give a general review of several good films:

(Nanjing) Bird of Paradise

— Ming

Among all the films released on New Year's Day, Bird of Paradise can be considered the best. This film has been introduced in various magazines or publications very early. It is a tragedy that describes the tragedy caused by etiquette [superstition] and more painfully talks about the racial boundaries between whites and natives. At the end, the girl sacrificed her life, making the love even more great. This is also the best work of director King Vidor's life. Even the digressions don't make the audience relax for a second. The natural and magnificent scenery has a lot of beauty in the midst of landslides and tsunamis. The position of the camera is also very clever. The swimming scenes are really like paintings. Dolores del Rio's romantic and private feelings make the script even more tragic. Her humorous expressions and fluent native language can perhaps be called "divine." Joe McCrea also has an amazing performance.

(Carlton) · · · Wandering Paris

— Yan Nan

Warner's comedy stars Al Olsen and Johnson may be unknown to everyone, but the public screening of "Soo,Ooo,Ooo Frenchmen" has raised their value to some extent. There are many dialogues in this film, but few jokes. There is neither singing nor dancing. Therefore, the comedic parts rely entirely on unconscious small movements and "relaxed" performances. The plot is good, and it cleverly describes how to view life as a child's play. In terms of directing, the ability is more than adequate. The photography light and cloth are the most beautiful because they are all five-colored. The actors are very average, and each person can represent the special personality of a certain class of people. At the same time, it also secretly satirizes the magic of money in modern society. Among comedies, this film can be called the best.

(New Light) ··· Silver Star's Success Story by Yan Nan

According to general conversations about me, it seems that "Silver Star's Success Story" (What Price Hollywood) is a mediocre film. However, in my opinion, it should be classified as above average. The reason it may not be popular with most people is likely due to the excessive dialogue, yet the dialogue is very brilliant and cannot be omitted. Constance Bennett has made even more progress in this film than in her previous works, artistically progressing in layers as she imitates a girl who is new to the film industry. The song she sings is very commendable, and Neil Hamilton is also extremely competent. Lowell Sherman's unrestrained frankness evokes indescribable feelings. He reveals the emotions of triumph and failure step by step, like mercury seeping into every crevice. His performance before and after is like two different people. Another merit of the film is its candid depiction of the real lives of people in the film industry. The work on the set is more authentic than any other film with Hollywood as a backdrop.

(New Light) ···· The Murders in the Rue Morgue

— Jie

"The Murders in the Rue Morgue" is a very famous detective novel, and its film adaptation is equally extraordinary. It is not purely a detective film. It has frightening elements; the kind of terror, mystery, and tension can be said to surpass "Frankenstein," yet in reality, this film is also reasonable. The director's skill is commendable, not only keeping ordinary audiences restless but also giving those who have read the novel a sense of "unfathomable" trembling. The entire lighting and photography focus on darkness and horror. Large shadows and urgent shouts have the beauty of a dragon appearing and disappearing. The plot also does its best to create "one wave after another." Bela Lugosi is very capable of displaying his instincts, and every move he makes stirs the audience's psychology. Sidney Fox also has some good points. If you want to tighten your mood, then this is a film not to be missed. It gives you more to savor than a musical or romance film.

Reader Opinions

"Go to the Countryside"

— Qu Pingnu

After reading Mr. Daosheng's article "The Need for Rural Cinemas" in the 22nd issue of this publication, I felt very happy.

Who dares to say that people in the countryside do not enjoy entertainment? Look, whenever there is a play at the temple, isn't it always crowded? At the same time, we can also hear news of rural people fighting with actors, supposedly because the actors made mistakes in the play. From this, it can be seen that rural people are as familiar with plays as city dwellers.

Movies are noble entertainment and noble art. Now, they are even recognized as a tool for social education, taking the lead in all kinds of entertainment.

As for its establishment, I feel that building a large cinema in the countryside is completely unrealistic in the current Chinese countryside. Therefore, we don't need to do that. I think there are many large drying grounds in the countryside besides fields and houses. I think we can use these to set up open-air cinemas. As for cold weather, we can use temples and ancestral halls to screen movies. As for equipment, I don't think it needs to be too fancy. Electric fans and water heaters are not necessary. Even the seats can be ordinary. I think as long as we aim to reduce costs, we can make it so that they only have to pay a few copper coins to watch. Only then can it be popularized. This is indeed a new path for the film industry. I hope comrades will quickly "go to the countryside!"

Wang Renmei Helps Out Temporarily

— Ji Zhong

Wang Renmei, of "Wild Rose," with her fluent performance and lively demeanor, has now become a first-class silver star. Now, due to the persuasion of Zheng Yingshi and Wang Fuqing of Hengsheng Company, she has temporarily agreed to join the cast of "Spring Tide." The film originally had two female leads. One is a romantic female role, already taken by Ms. Li Li. But the role of the lively girl who ultimately succeeds in love in the play has not been resolved until now. Now, Miss Wang has agreed to help out.

The 1932 Hollywood Balance Sheet

— Luo Xiu

Every year, Hollywood is customarily assessed by the Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences to determine the best performing stars and award medals. Last year (1932), the best performing stars were announced; the female star was Mantlet Laishuo, and the male star was Leah Byron Moore. Everyone in Hollywood agrees that this is appropriate.

Others, such as the stars who are most bombarded by newspapers, have also been decided. First is Jean Harlow, due to the tragic death of her husband, Paul Bern. Second is Charlie Chaplin, who circumnavigated the globe. And Greta Garbo is listed third.

The richest star is considered to be Chaplin, just the tax he pays on stocks and bonds amounts to seven million, six hundred and eighty-seven thousand, five hundred and seventy gold yuan. Mary Pickford, although she has had few works recently, is listed second, and her husband, Douglas Fairbanks, is third. They are indeed the richest family among the stars.

The Editor

The Story of the "Match King" (2)

— Translated by Xi Meng

Paul's rise did not stop there. This foreman had a daughter named Beibei. She was very beautiful, and in Paul's eyes, she looked like an angel from heaven. Soon, Beibei was also bewitched by Paul, deeply imprinting Paul in her tender heart.

One day, Paul went to the foreman's house. Her bright eyes looked at Paul's face, as if there were unspoken words of love she wanted to pour out to Paul. The foreman was drunk, so happy that he was beside himself. When he saw Paul come in, he shouted loudly.

"This kid is extremely clever. Beibei, do you know who earns the money you deposit in the bank for me every week? Who? Haha, no one, no one earns it. I now have eight names on the list. The owners of those names don't know if they exist in this world. They are all fictitious brothers. Haha, there are eight ghosts, wearing white uniforms, working for Paul and me. Isn't that interesting? This wonderful plan was all thought up by Paul." After he finished speaking, he stumbled drunkenly into the bedroom to find the Duke of Zhou (to sleep). This left Paul and Beibei alone.

"This drunken old man," Paul began, "but this is not a long-term plan either. Sweetheart, how much money is in the bank after all?"

"Four hundred and sixty yuan," she told him softly, her peach cheeks pressed tightly against his face. "Paul, be careful. If he finds out, he will definitely put me to death, and he will definitely kill you too."

"Baby, don't worry. Don't panic until things come to a head. I'll naturally think of something." He kissed her lips and let her go. The drunken old man inside was shouting:

"Beibei."

"It's getting late, I have to go," Paul said goodbye. He finished speaking and left.

Paul returned to his bedroom in the thieves' nest, muttering to himself and calculating the old man's four hundred and sixty yuan, plus his own... a letter was stuffed in from under the door. Paul picked it up, opened it, and looked at it. The letter was from Paul's uncle in Sweden. His uncle owned a small match factory in Sweden. He said in the letter that he was very sorry, he knew that Paul's career in the United States was great, and he did not dare to bother him with small matters, but because he was old, he couldn't manage the factory very well. However, if Paul could not forget his humble family and would kindly come, he would definitely be able to give him some good lessons so that his failing business could be maintained.

Paul hurriedly found a newspaper and flipped to the shipping schedule to Europe. The next day, he secretly went to meet Beibei. On the third day, he was waiting for Beibei across from the bank again. After a while, Beibei came. She stuffed a roll of banknotes into Paul's hand. He could feel Beibei trembling with fear.

"Sweetheart, why are you so timid?" he said. "By the time we leave this place tens of thousands of miles away, I'm afraid that old man still won't know. But it's getting late, you hurry back and pack your things."

"Paul!" Beibei shouted in surprise. She hugged his arm. "Do you love me? Do you really love me?"
